    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9258912210400840623"><i>It happened like this. I was stolen from an airport. Taken from everything I knew, everything I was used to. Taken to sand and heat, dirt and danger. And he expected me to love him.<br/><br/> This is my story.<br/><br/> A letter from nowhere.</i><br/><br/>Sixteen-year-old Gemma is kidnapped from Bangkok airport and taken to the Australian Outback. This wild and desolate landscape becomes almost a character</span>
  <span id="freeText9258912210400840623" style="display:none"><i>It happened like this. I was stolen from an airport. Taken from everything I knew, everything I was used to. Taken to sand and heat, dirt and danger. And he expected me to love him.<br /><br /> This is my story.<br /><br /> A letter from nowhere.</i><br /><br />Sixteen-year-old Gemma is kidnapped from Bangkok airport and taken to the Australian Outback. This wild and desolate landscape becomes almost a character in the book, so vividly is it described. Ty, her captor, is no stereotype. He is young, fit and completely gorgeous. This new life in the wilderness has been years in the planning. He loves only her, wants only her. Under the hot glare of the Australian sun, cut off from the world outside, can the force of his love make Gemma love him back? <br /><br />The story takes the form of a letter, written by Gemma to Ty, reflecting on those strange and disturbing months in the outback. Months when the lines between love and obsession, and love and dependency, blur until they don't exist—almost.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9258912210400840623" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Because you followed Gemma's journey. You felt what she felt. The desire. The desire to not have desire, but still having desire. You wanted Ty just a<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Because you followed Gemma's journey. You felt what she felt. The desire. The desire to not have desire, but still having desire. You wanted Ty just as badly as she did.<br /><br />You had Stockholm syndrome. THAT'S why you wanted to cry.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=issue">issue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=psychology">psychology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104727472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17274870581090410863">When I was a teenager, I remember watching a movie with my family and the couple onscreen kissed for the first time and of course five seconds later were sleeping together. My dad, trying to keep the morality of four teenage girls intact, complained about movies always doing that, making you root for something you didn't believe in. I remember thinking "it's just a movie; you're supposed to want that," because I had wanted it.<br/><br/>Christopher is a smart woman. She realizes this power, that as an auth</span>
  <span id="freeText17274870581090410863" style="display:none">When I was a teenager, I remember watching a movie with my family and the couple onscreen kissed for the first time and of course five seconds later were sleeping together. My dad, trying to keep the morality of four teenage girls intact, complained about movies always doing that, making you root for something you didn't believe in. I remember thinking "it's just a movie; you're supposed to want that," because I had wanted it.<br /><br />Christopher is a smart woman. She realizes this power, that as an author, she can direct you in what you're supposed to want, who you're supposed to like, and what ending you're supposed to root for. And she uses it to mess with your head. Ty and Gemma are basically the only characters in the book, so you <i>want</i> them to end up together. Ty is a kidnapper and has a temper, but he's a kind, likable kidnapper. From the beginning, you want Gemma to get over it and like Ty. He had a sad life and has such a vulnerable quality and if only Gemma would love him it would make him all better. You see what Christopher does? She makes you, the reader, experience Stockholm syndrome, so that by the end you're as conflicted as Gemma about the outcome and about your own feelings of Gemma's resistance and Ty's culpability. She makes you consider Stockholm syndrome from the inside. That's brilliant.<br /><br />ETA: I have several friends who didn't like the book and it's made me think about why this works so well for some and not for others. It comes down to you. If you're the type of girl who'd want to protect a broken spirit then you'll fall right into the trap that is Ty's charm. If you like a man's man and have no patience for weak men, the book won't work for you. The book may have been more powerful had we fallen in love with a man who was a little bit rough, a little bit forceful, a little bit cruel and yet Gemma depended on him for her survival. But maybe not. It would have been more of a risk and may not have had the same longing for romance that this has. Either way, it still requires you the reader to pull off the full affect. It's a risk and sometimes it pays off. Sometimes it doesn't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17274870581090410863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_121859396" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121859396" />
    <a title="Lyndsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4224396-lyndsey"><img alt="Lyndsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288890060p2/4224396.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121859396?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyndsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyndsey" href="/user/show/4224396-lyndsey">Lyndsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=reviewed-5-stars">reviewed-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=reviewed-2010">reviewed-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121859396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6734034595744015288">This book completely reaffirmed my fascination with the beautiful land that is <b>Australia</b>.<br/><br/>But the people who live there seem to want everyone to think it's a lot like <i>this</i>:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339528i/696257.jpg' width='319' height='283' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Or this:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339528i/696258.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Or even this:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339528i/696259.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Gemma, just a regular 16 year old school girl, has been captured by a handsome and alluring young Australian man named Ty. Although Gemma seems to think so, it never feels like she's in any imminent danger, from Ty at least. From the environment - yes.<br/><br/>The stakes and suspense don't seem that high, as I fully</span>
  <span id="freeText6734034595744015288" style="display:none">This book completely reaffirmed my fascination with the beautiful land that is <b>Australia</b>.<br><br>But the people who live there seem to want everyone to think it's a lot like <i>this</i>:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339528i/696257.jpg" width="319" height="283" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Or this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339528i/696258.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Or even this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339528i/696259.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Gemma, just a regular 16 year old school girl, has been captured by a handsome and alluring young Australian man named Ty. Although Gemma seems to think so, it never feels like she's in any imminent danger, from Ty at least. From the environment - yes.<br><br>The stakes and suspense don't seem that high, as I fully believed that he never intended to hurt her. Regardless, the author managed to draw me in with every single word.<br><br>The story itself is incredible, as is the the writing and character development. I just worry that it's glorifying kidnapping. <i>Cause really, how many child abductors are 20-something sexy Australian men with supermodel looks and a hot bod, who only want to be loved?</i> If I was Gemma, I can't say I would mind.<br><br>I mean, I picture him looking a bit like this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339528i/696260.jpg" width="319" height="410" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Whoopsie!! Not the right picture! That's from my <i>secret</i> stash... *blushes*</b><br><br>Here the <u>right</u> one:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339528i/696261.jpg" width="319" height="405" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But our girl is very stubborn and never seems to be giving up on getting away from him. She's resilient and strong and everything you expect the heroine of a young adult novel to be.<br><br>And whew! The male lead character Ty, our captor, is really hot. Come on, Gemma. The scene with the paint where he leans in and asks (referring to the paint of course) <i>"Do you want some?"</i> I couldn't help but think heeeeeeeeck yeah.<br><br><u>I imagine if any other girl in the world had been there, she'd be jumping up and down with her hand raised saying "I do, I do."</u><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339528i/696262.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Ty is extremely charming and a bit of a paradox.</b> He is multiple layered character, who although seems unsocial and outdoorsy, is good with words and can completely make you swoon.<br><br>Though most of this is a result of brilliant writing, a lot it also comes from the talented narrator of the audio book.<br><br>I know the book alone is amazing, <u>but this one is really worth listening to on audio</u>.<br><br>It is the most well read book I have listened to in a long time, probably EVER. The voice of Ty isn't even noticeable as being read by a women. The narrator and the author are both on the exact same wavelength and both nail the complex nature of our male lead as well as the strong willed Gemma.<br><br>I do wish things had gone a little differently in the end. I'm not sure that what Gemma did is fully representative of what a normal 16 year old would do, but I guess that what happened is what HAD to happen for the story. The romantic in me just wanted things to be different. I also think I'm suffering from Stockholm Syndrome even more so than Gemma was.<br><br>I know that a lot of people won't sympathize with Ty at all. But I'm a sucker for a man with a <i>hot bod and an Australian accent</i>.<br><br><b>Definitely, this is another of my favorite books I've read lately. And my favorite audiobook so far!</b></span>

<div id="review_111204411" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111204411" />
    <a title="Nina ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3785659-nina"><img alt="Nina ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326399105p2/3785659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111204411?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina ♥" href="/user/show/3785659-nina">Nina ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nina ♥ by: </span>
      Maggie Stiefvater
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3785659-nina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111204411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5675776441134044607"><i>"I made it," you said, gruffly, "for you."<br/>You shoved it onto my finger. It was roughly carved, shaped from a lump of something colourful and cold...a ring made entirely from a gemstone. It was beautiful. It glinted emerald greens and blood reds over my skin, and had tiny flecks of gold catching the light. I couldn't stop staring at it.<br/>"Why?" I asked.<br/>You didn't answer that. Instead you touched the ring gently and looked piercingly at me, unsaid questions in your eyes.</i><br/><br/>HOLY SHIT! I should <i>not</i> have </span>
  <span id="freeText5675776441134044607" style="display:none"><i>"I made it," you said, gruffly, "for you."<br />You shoved it onto my finger. It was roughly carved, shaped from a lump of something colourful and cold...a ring made entirely from a gemstone. It was beautiful. It glinted emerald greens and blood reds over my skin, and had tiny flecks of gold catching the light. I couldn't stop staring at it.<br />"Why?" I asked.<br />You didn't answer that. Instead you touched the ring gently and looked piercingly at me, unsaid questions in your eyes.</i><br /><br />HOLY SHIT! I should <i>not</i> have read this book! (Even though it's definitely going to be on top of my 'favorites' list.) I don't think I've ever cried so much while reading a book! But I loved it! It was perfect.<br /><br />I wanted to read this book for so long, but couldn't get my hands on it. I was just very fascinated by the summary of the book, and who am I to deny that beautiful cover? Well, the story begins with <i>"You saw me before I saw you."</i> Sounds intriguing, right? Well, it's like that from start to end of the book. So, Ty, kidnaps Gemma from an airport--putting drugs in her coffee so she wouldn't struggle--and takes her to a desert in Australia, where no one could find them. He has a whole life planned out for them both, thinking that Gemma would fall in love with him eventually. Throughout the book, Gemma tries (in vain) to escape, and the unusual thing is that Ty lets her. But soon, Gemma finds out she can't get out of there unless Ty will come with her, since he knows the desert better. As the story progresses, Gemma struggles with her feelings for Ty, especially when she found out that he was as desperate as she was, when she learns of his background.<br /><br />Ty was a very complex character. I never imagined to sympathize with a villain--if he could even be called a villain--much less one who kidnaps people, but Ty was such a sad, tragic character. There were times when I hated him for taking Gemma against her will, but when Gemma found out that she loved him, it was like I was falling for him right along with her. Seriously, it was like I was getting Stockholm Syndrome too! Lucy Christopher knows just how to mess with your mind. <br /><br />It was all like this to me: ...I love Ty, he's amazing...wait, no he's not, he's a stalker <i>and</i> a kidnapper...but he's so sweet!...let go of Gemma you controlling creep...Oh my gawd he's so effin' hot!... <br /><br />It's like having the devil and angel on your shoulder! So, yes, he kidnapped her. But he also loved her passionately. He knew he was going to go to prison, but he chose to stay by her side and save her. That's what I loved about him the most. The fact that he ran miles to save her life.<br /><br />Ugh, I'm getting conflicted again.<br /><br />Again, I can't really express my feelings about this book, but it was definitely <i>the most</i> intense book I've ever read. I couldn't put it down.<br /><br />I want Lucy Christopher to write a sequel. She <i>can't</i> leave it like this! But, at the same time I don't really want her to. It's actually the ending--that tear-jerking, heart-wrenching ending--that made the book so unique and unforgettable. I don't want that to be ruined.<br /><br />...I'm doing it again, aren't I? Dammit, I have to stop contracting myself. Makes me sound like a weirdo who has no idea what she's talking about.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5675776441134044607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_305434845" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/305434845" />
    <a title="Inge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6278820-inge"><img alt="Inge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556214992p2/6278820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/305434845?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Inge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Inge" href="/user/show/6278820-inge">Inge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer305434845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16740198915940093316"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>… that’s it?<br/><br/><a href='http://tinypic.com?ref=11ghppc' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374010ra/727897.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Well, that was a shit fucking letter, wasn’t it? Can you even call that a letter? It’s just a recollection of everything that happened between Gemma and Ty. As if someone would be able to remember every conversation that had happened on every day for a month. It’s fine as a story, but I did not accept the letter concept. It reminds me of a certain <i>Friends</i> episode where Rachel and Ross are fighting and Rachel wrote him a letter.<br/><br/><b>Ross:</b> “I fell asleep!”<br/><b>Rachel:</b> “You fell <i>aslee</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16740198915940093316" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br><br>… that’s it?<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=11ghppc" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374010ra/727897.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Well, that was a shit fucking letter, wasn’t it? Can you even call that a letter? It’s just a recollection of everything that happened between Gemma and Ty. As if someone would be able to remember every conversation that had happened on every day for a month. It’s fine as a story, but I did not accept the letter concept. It reminds me of a certain <i>Friends</i> episode where Rachel and Ross are fighting and Rachel wrote him a letter.<br><br><b>Ross:</b> “I fell asleep!”<br><b>Rachel:</b> “You fell <i>asleep</i>?!”<br><b>Ross:</b> “It was 5:30 in the morning, and you had rambled on for 18 pages. <i>Front and back</i>!”<br><br>I think it’s safe to say that my expectations were way up high, because of all the skyrocketing ratings, and it all came crashing down into a million pieces. I thought this book was going to be fucked up, all kinds of twisted, but luckily for Gemma she met the world’s most docile kidnapper in the history of time. Sure, he followed her for a couple years, but he actually took good care of her and didn’t force her into anything. He had expected her to love his little place in the middle of nowhere. I mean, who wouldn’t love living in a fucking desert, away from every type of civilisation, hunting camels and kangaroos and possibly being bitten by poisonous snakes? But when Gemma keeps whining, he promises that he’ll take her back to the real world if she still doesn’t love it after four months.<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2lstidz" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374010ra/727898.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>That sure is convenient. But hey, we are supposed to like Ty, right? He’s given these bright blue eyes and a tight body so we’ll swoon over him, and a dramatic back-story and a guilty conscience so we can feel sorry for him. He <i>loves</i> Gemma, in his own twisted way. He means well; all he wants is company, never mind the fact that his company is there against her will. But hey, he’s actually a pretty nice guy, so he doesn’t force his company on Gemma, which results in one of the most boring books I have ever read. <i>Nothing</i> happens. They just live alongside each other and have awkward conversations. Hell, if I want awkward conversations <i>I’ll</i> talk to someone. While you guys are swooning over Ty, can you still remember that he actually kidnapped a girl and once fenced her in like cattle? Because he didn’t give a rat’s ass about Gemma when he took her away “for ever”. I’m just saying ‘cause Gemma seemed to be forgetting all that as we got nearer to the ending, even falling asleep in his arms and wanting to kiss him. At the end, he’s just another pretty boy. But a weird little fucker at that – <i>he paints his penis</i>. Do I need to say more?<br><br>Then comes the ending and <i>because of a snake bite</i> Gemma ends up being rescued. Ty decides to take her back to the real world to save her life, knowing that he’ll end up in prison. Once again, thank fuck for Gemma being abducted by such a <i>gentleman</i>. She even kisses him on the cheek in the end and <i>thanks him</i> for showing her some beautiful landscape. Are you fucking kidding me with this? “Yes, you may have kidnapped me and I hate you, but I love you too and it sure was beautiful over there.” Girl, you need help. I understand Stockholm Syndrome and it really fascinates me, but this just wasn’t done well. Gemma’s writing was boring and detached and it left me feeling completely empty of any feelings other than anger.<br><br>Because I am angry. I am sorely disappointed and, well, fuck this book. Snape is not amused.<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2dt9hd5" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374010ra/727899.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16740198915940093316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111089338" />
    <a title="Maggie Stiefvater" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1246837-maggie-stiefvater"><img alt="Maggie Stiefvater" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587234846p2/1246837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111089338?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie Stiefvater" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie Stiefvater" href="/user/show/1246837-maggie-stiefvater">Maggie Stiefvater</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1246837-maggie-stiefvater?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1246837-maggie-stiefvater?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111089338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1392178614108853118">I just had a copy of STOLEN by Lucy Christopher put into my hands at ALA, and I am definitely, definitely sending a quote for them to use for the paperback edition. It’s a YA novel about a girl who is kidnapped from an airport by a crazy guy and taken to a shack in the Australian outback. The novel features<br/><br/>1) crazy guy<br/>2) camels<br/>3) strong heroine<br/>4) poisonous snakes! (did you know that Australia is the only continent where species of poisonous snakes outnumbers non-poisonous ones?)<br/>5) hallucinating<br/>6</span>
  <span id="freeText1392178614108853118" style="display:none">I just had a copy of STOLEN by Lucy Christopher put into my hands at ALA, and I am definitely, definitely sending a quote for them to use for the paperback edition. It’s a YA novel about a girl who is kidnapped from an airport by a crazy guy and taken to a shack in the Australian outback. The novel features<br /><br />1) crazy guy<br />2) camels<br />3) strong heroine<br />4) poisonous snakes! (did you know that Australia is the only continent where species of poisonous snakes outnumbers non-poisonous ones?)<br />5) hallucinating<br />6) kangaroos<br />7) psychological terror and thrillingness!<br />8) vehicular chases<br />9) did I mention crazy guy?<br />10) a supporting cast of chickens<br /><br />It’s got a great sense of place and the character development is just fantastic (I love me some trauma), but the thing I liked best was that as Gemma, the main character, spends more time in the presence of her kidnapper, the author very, very, very skillfully messes with our brains just like Gemma’s brain is getting messed with. It makes for a very complex read with no easy answers, just like I like ‘em. I loved how all of the motivations were thoroughly grounded in past history; we get a profile of the kidnapper as a human, not just as a stick figure. As a teen, I would have adored this book even more. My only complaint? It reads a little long in places, but I think that may have been my deadlines speaking more than the book’s shortfall. I know there will be many that say that this isn't how most kidnappings go down and tell you to go read LIVING DEAD GIRL instead, but I don't believe that books need to tell the most common story -- just the one most interesting to the author. Highly recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1392178614108853118" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_102582666" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102582666" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102582666?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=i-learned-something-new">i-learned-something-new</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=leaves-awesomeness-behind">leaves-awesomeness-behind</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102582666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13297046347915168440">Stolen is such a singular reading experience that its difficult to decide how I feel about it.<br/><br/>Gemma is a sixteen year old English girl kidnapped by Ty and taken into the Western Australian outback where she is held prisoner.<br/><br/>I had to give this book five stars for several reasons. One of the reasons is because it was so fantastically well written. Beautiful, touching, heart breaking and real. Christopher doesn't spare on the details both good and bad. Never before have I felt a book to be so real,</span>
  <span id="freeText13297046347915168440" style="display:none">Stolen is such a singular reading experience that its difficult to decide how I feel about it.<br /><br />Gemma is a sixteen year old English girl kidnapped by Ty and taken into the Western Australian outback where she is held prisoner.<br /><br />I had to give this book five stars for several reasons. One of the reasons is because it was so fantastically well written. Beautiful, touching, heart breaking and real. Christopher doesn't spare on the details both good and bad. Never before have I felt a book to be so real, so gritty and tangible.<br /><br />This book is a journey into the world of Stockholm Syndrome and the craft of Christopher's skill left even me, feeling the effects of this baffling psychological problem.<br /><br />The characters of Ty and Gemma are fantastic. At first I was frustrated with Gemma. I was so used to reading kick-ass female protagonists who could do anything that it was aggravating to be stuck with a sixteen year old who was incapable and terror stricken. Yet she gets to you. Her pain, her struggles. She's a real sixteen year old. This isn't some fantasy character that can do everything. Yet she has a sense of will and spirit. Perhaps her defining characteristic is the truth that she is willing to tell herself - completely and honestly.<br /><br />Ty is also amazing as a character. He is equal parts scary, confused, angry, hostile, delusional. He is also beautiful, gentle, capable, intense and loving. He is such a mixed bag of all these things.<br /><br />If you're looking for action and suspense in this book - you won't find it. Yet I personally found the strength of the characters and the outback itself was strong enough to carry this story without needing a great deal of edge-of-your-seat intensity. The mental intensity was enough for me. <br /><br />Others may find this story boring but I found it touching and amazing. I highly recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13297046347915168440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_460092376" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/460092376" />
    <a title="Rosalinda *KRASNORADA*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada"><img alt="Rosalinda *KRASNORADA*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583582487p2/12788865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/460092376?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosalinda *KRASNORADA*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosalinda *KRASNORADA*" href="/user/show/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada">Rosalinda *KRASNORADA*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada?shelf=i-need-more-stars">i-need-more-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada?shelf=best-book-ever">best-book-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada?shelf=perfect-hero-and-heroine">perfect-hero-and-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada?shelf=intelligent-heroine">intelligent-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada?shelf=loved-loved-loved-it">loved-loved-loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada?shelf=brits-i-love-you">brits-i-love-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12788865-rosalinda-krasnorada?shelf=need-more-like-now">need-more-like-now</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460092376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6057535112161358414"><br/><br/><b> ----------------HYPERVENTILATING------------------<br/>-------------------AUGUST 2013 UPDATE--------------<br/><br/>Look what I just saw on Lucy's FB:<br/><br/>Lucy Christopher<br/>If I tell you I'm about to fly to San Diego to work on the screenplay of Stolen .... would you be excited?<br/>Me gusta · · Compartir · 83 · Hace 3 minutos · <br/><br/><br/>OMFG!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! WHERE CAN I BUY MY TICKETS????!!!! NEED THAT FILM LIKE YESTERDAY!!!!<br/><br/>P.S. Sorry for updating an old review but this was soooooo good for me that I had to do it!<br/>------------</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6057535112161358414" style="display:none"><br><br><b> ----------------HYPERVENTILATING------------------<br>-------------------AUGUST 2013 UPDATE--------------<br><br>Look what I just saw on Lucy's FB:<br><br>Lucy Christopher<br>If I tell you I'm about to fly to San Diego to work on the screenplay of Stolen .... would you be excited?<br>Me gusta · · Compartir · 83 · Hace 3 minutos · <br><br><br>OMFG!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! WHERE CAN I BUY MY TICKETS????!!!! NEED THAT FILM LIKE YESTERDAY!!!!<br><br>P.S. Sorry for updating an old review but this was soooooo good for me that I had to do it!<br>-------------------------------------------------------------------<br><br><br>***FULL REVIEW NOW UP***<br><br>FIVE BEAUTIFUL &amp; HEARTBREAKING AUSTRALIAN STARS </b><br><br>Could I have loved this book anymore? <b>NO</b><br><br>Would I change anything about their story? <b>Hell NO</b><br><br>Do I need a sequel even if I know I won't probably get it? <b>Yes, please with sugar on top! </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398184i/769325.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I bought this book AGES ago but I didn't want to read it because I knew how it ended. And I didn't mind <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ this didn't have a HEA  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I just lost the interest because I know what would happen. Anyway, Basuhi read it last week and she loved it so I thought it was time to give it a try, even if YA is not a genre I read a lot lately. <br><br>This is the story of Gemma &amp; Ty. Gemma is a 16 years old girl from London who is traveling with her parents. She is in Bangkok airport waiting for her flight and she meets Ty, a 25 years old guy who has coffee with her.<br><br>When I read the blurb of this book I always thought about KISS ME by Ed Sheeran but now that I have finished the book I can say this song is just for them:<br><br><blockquote>
<b><br>I've fallen for your eyes<br>But they don't know me yet<br><br>And the feeling I forget<br>I'm in love now<br><br>Kiss me like you wanna be loved<br>Wanna be loved<br>Wanna be loved <br></b> </blockquote><br><br>The thing is Gemma is having coffee with this beautiful guy one minute and the next one someone has drugged her. She just doesn't know where she is and she doesn't know what happened but she wakes up in the middle of nowhere... (I would say the middle of paradise, but I understand she doesn't see it that way).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398275i/769542.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was scared this was going to be boring, I mean, I almost knew <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ they didn't even kiss  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but boy, I was waaaaaaaaay wrong, I didn't even need it.<br><br>I know, a lot of my GR buddies cannot like a story about a kidnapper (yes, I am thinking about you Baba) but this is one is way different and I know most of my buddies don’t read YA anyway but I just wanted to say that Ty is not the typical kidnapper. He NEVER put a hand on Gemma, EVER forced her to do anything. He obviously had a problem, I understand and accept that what he did was WRONG but he always respected her even if he didn’t respect her freedom.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>”How long will you keep me?”<br>“For ever, of course” </b>
</blockquote><br><br>At the beginning, I couldn’t help it, I thought he was freaking insane but I ended up understanding some things about him and I really think he was in love with her and he just wanted her to love that land as much as he did. He did it the wrong way which is a shame.<br><br>But I also agreed with him sometimes, even if the way he did things was NOT correct.<br><br><blockquote>
<b>”I like cities”<br>“No one’s real in a city. Nothing’s real” </b> </blockquote><br><br>Gemma hates him, she just wants to escape, she doesn’t have any kind of feelings for him at all during a good part of the book. And that is what I also loved. If I imagine myself in a situation like that I cannot believe I could be able to have feelings for my kidnapper the next day I have been kidnapped, that is NOT real. <b>Gemma was very real, there was not even one second that she didn’t try to scape from him but at the same time she was curious about him, about his life, about why he was so fucked up so she gave in and started talking to him.</b><br><br>When the author starts telling us more about Ty you can’t help it and you feel sorry for him because he didn’t have an easy life. I am not saying I think he did the right thing but I can understand why he was so fucked up.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398275i/769543.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><blockquote>”They just wanted recognition, they wanted to fit in... it’s what most people want”<br>“Excepts freaks like you”<br>“I want freedom” </blockquote> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398275i/769544.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ty explains Gemma how he met her, why she was the perfect person to go with him to that land and even though, I repeat that he did the wrong thing, he had his reasons. Ok, he kidnapped her but he also saved her <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ from Josh, years before  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398275i/769545._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Every single part of the landscape and every single animal was a character of this book. The story with the Camel was maybe the kind of story that Ty was expecting to have with Gemma. His “baby steps” worked with the Camel…<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>”We’re getting there. Baby steps"</blockquote>
</b><br>But you know what? Those baby steps <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ also worked with Gemma, even if she was stubborn  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b><blockquote> “Pain means it’s healing” </blockquote> </b><br><br>Gemma knows he is not that bad but she stills can’t trust him. She just wants to escape, at all costs and he only wants her there, even for a few months because he is convinced that she will end up loving that place as much as he does.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>”It’s just… to survive this land, you need to love it. And that takes time. Right now, you need me”<br>“I know” </blockquote>
</b><br><br>But she cannot help it either and she starts caring for him, she tries to understand or help him, even if she knows he is doing the wrong thing.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>”People love what they’re used to, I guess”<br>“No. PEOPLE SHOULD LOVE WHAT NEEDS LOVING. That way they can save it” </blockquote>
</b><br><br>Wow, this was one of my favourite quotes of the book. So true!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398275i/769546.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved the way Ty showed her his love for that land, for his paints. The way he respected the oldfellas. Ty is seriously like a perfect guy. I know he had issues but he was PURE, he was a good person.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398275i/769547.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And finally Gemma started enjoying his company, she stopped running away from him, ignoring him.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>You smiled, your eyes crinkling at the corners. I looked away quickly, wanting to hold your gaze but knowing I shouldn’t.<br>Right at that moment it was as if we were the only two people left in the whole world.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398275i/769548._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>”And how long will we sit here like this? Just another moment, or the rest of our lives? You know which one I’d prefer</blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398275i/769549.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>******SPOILERS AHEAD******</b><br><br>And yeah, shit got real as usual. But you know what? Ty proved he was a good person once again because he never hesitated, he decided to save her life, <b>NO MATTER WHAT</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398275i/769550._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><blockquote> “Why?”<br>You didn’t answer that. Instead you touched the ring gently and looked piercingly at me, unsaid questions in your eyes. </blockquote> </b><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ When Gem is safe in the hospital she misses Ty, she misses their moments together. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>It’s hard to hate someone once you understand them<br><br><blockquote>But I hated you for something else too. Right then, and at every moment <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ since you’d left me  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> in that apartment . I wanted your arms around me, your face close to mine. I wanted your smell. And I knew <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I couldn’t  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - shouldn’t – have it. That’s what I hated most. The uncertainty of you. You’d kidnapped me, put my life in danger… but I <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ loved you too. Or thought I did  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. None of it made sense. </blockquote> </b><br><br>And Gemma finally accepts she did love that land, she did appreciate those days, she did <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ love Ty  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398275i/769551.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <blockquote> And let’s face it, you did steal me. But you saved my life too. And somewhere in the middle, you showed me a place so different and beautiful, I can never get it out of my mind. And I can’t get you out of there either. You’re stuck in my brain like my own blood vessels</blockquote>
</b><br><br>I loved Gemma, because she always knew and understood what was wrong and what was right. Because she wasn’t selfish, because she defended the truth, because she was sensible.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>You told me once of the plants that lie dormant through the drought; that wait, half dead, deep in the earth. The plants that wait for the rain. You said they’d wait for years, if they had to; that they’d almost kill themselves before they grew again. But as soon as those first drops of water fall, those plants begin to stretch and spread their roots. They travel up through the soil and sand to reach the surface. There’s a chance for them again </blockquote>
</b><br><br>I love how the author ends her acknowledgments:<br><br><b>As Ty says, this is a land that needs love and ‘needs saving’</b><br><br>Is that love or Stockholm Syndrome? I want to believe this was a love story…<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <span id="freeText6713999715766463587" style="display:none">Five stars. <br /><br />I really don't know how to feel right now. <br />I feel so sad, but that isn't the right word to explain how I feel about this book. <br />It's so complicated. I hated some of the moments in this book- could not even begin to imagine myself feeling even the slightest bit of empathy for certain characters. Yet, something about this book pulls you in and flips you over. Before you know it, you're viewing this book in an entirely different light than when you started it. Suddenly, your eyes have opened to the true heart of this book, and you understand. You understand the message it carries, and the weight of it all. <br />It's confusing how this book makes you feel so much compassion for something so terribly wrong. That's the entire point though. <br />The problem is, by the time you've grasped it all, it's too late. The story ends, and like Gemma, you find your heart aching for everything you finally understand. <br /><br />Yes, this book is complicated. And confusing. And a storm of emotions. <br />It's also beautiful. And captivating. And so, so breathtakingly real. <br />This is the kind of story that will stick with you. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10672082552079019370">I'm still crying as I type this.<br/><br/>This review will very likely be brief and will very likely be a hot mess, because . . . I just can't believe how gorgeous this single piece of literature is. I can't believe it took me this long to read it. I'll definitely say it was worth the wait, though.<br/><br/>It's been a while since I've read something that touched me this deeply. How this book is written just gutted me and left me breathless at times. Gemma was relatable because she was a <i>real</i> teenage girl. I would'</span>
  <span id="freeText10672082552079019370" style="display:none">I'm still crying as I type this.<br /><br />This review will very likely be brief and will very likely be a hot mess, because . . . I just can't believe how gorgeous this single piece of literature is. I can't believe it took me this long to read it. I'll definitely say it was worth the wait, though.<br /><br />It's been a while since I've read something that touched me this deeply. How this book is written just gutted me and left me breathless at times. Gemma was relatable because she was a <i>real</i> teenage girl. I would've done some of the things she did if I were in her position, and I would've thought of things the same way she did. She was always wary, always looking for chances of escape, even though it was pretty much hopeless.<br /><br />And then there's Ty.<br /><br />I wasn't expecting to be so in love with him. I wasn't expecting this at all. But even less than 100 pages in, I had already warmed up to him. He is not evil or cruel in any way. He is broken and lonely and fuck I have tears landing on the backs of my hands.<br /><br />The last parts were really the parts that hit me. Deep. I loved how this book ended. I loved everything about this book and oh my god forget about all those books that I've said are the best books I've ever read because this one tops every fucking list. I'm not kidding.<br /><br />Okay, I don't know what else to type anymore, I'm sorry. I just . . . god, you guys, this book. This fucking book.</span>

<div id="review_102735046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102735046" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102735046?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545170932" href="/book/show/7092412-stolen">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      Kat, Penny and just about everyone else I know on GR
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=printz">printz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=aus-nz">aus-nz</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102735046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14091596139575446244">It is with sadness I am giving <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6408862.Stolen' title='Stolen by Lucy Christopher' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stolen</a> an "it was ok" 2-star rating. I expected to love this book. What's not to love? The premise was right up my alley - a psychological thriller, an exploration of Stockholm Syndrome, a story about a kidnapped person who finds herself emotionally attached to her captor. It's a treasure for a reader like me, fascinated by crazy and sick. But somehow <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6408862.Stolen' title='Stolen by Lucy Christopher' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stolen</a> didn't move me in any significant way.<br/><br/>While I found the premise to be extremely interesting and pretty much </span>
  <span id="freeText14091596139575446244" style="display:none">It is with sadness I am giving <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6408862.Stolen" title="Stolen by Lucy Christopher" rel="nofollow noopener">Stolen</a> an "it was ok" 2-star rating. I expected to love this book. What's not to love? The premise was right up my alley - a psychological thriller, an exploration of Stockholm Syndrome, a story about a kidnapped person who finds herself emotionally attached to her captor. It's a treasure for a reader like me, fascinated by crazy and sick. But somehow <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6408862.Stolen" title="Stolen by Lucy Christopher" rel="nofollow noopener">Stolen</a> didn't move me in any significant way.<br /><br />While I found the premise to be extremely interesting and pretty much a genius idea on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2903247.Lucy_Christopher" title="Lucy Christopher" rel="nofollow noopener">Lucy Christopher</a>'s part, I thought the execution of this idea was lacking. <br /><br />A book which centers on intricacies of human psychology <b>ought</b> to have realistic characters. Neither Gemma nor Ty ever came alive for me and therefore the entire journey of Gemma's to form an attachment to her kidnapper never worked IMO. Neither did I have any feelings for Ty and his sad-sad life stories. I saw how the author tried to make him somewhat attractive and worthy of compassion, but for me Ty remained a creep from the beginning till the very end.<br /><br />I also found that the letter format (which I love) of the novel didn't quite work. Normally letters tend to give me an upclose understanding of the characters who write them, but in this case Gemma stayed anonymous and distant throughout the story. Endless "I"s and "you"s drove me nuts too. <br /><br />I still think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6408862.Stolen" title="Stolen by Lucy Christopher" rel="nofollow noopener">Stolen</a> is a great discussion book. Penny brought up a particularly interesting topic in her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102684032" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a> about a disturbing trend in YA literature to portray unhealthy relationships as romantic. For me personally the book was spoiled by poor characterization, overwhelming telling instead of showing, and boring pacing. It will sound harsh, but I don't think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2903247.Lucy_Christopher" title="Lucy Christopher" rel="nofollow noopener">Lucy Christopher</a> is a good writer and I don't think she knows human nature enough to undertake such topic. <br /><br />My opinion is in a minority however, so maybe you should pick up the book and judge it for yourself. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14091596139575446244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=v-emotionally-moving">v-emotionally-moving</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1822445246" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17892817275658504695">BR with my girl <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069-pragya' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pragya!</a> <s>I can't belive she feels nothing for Ty.</s> <br/><br/>How can you recover from a book that rips your heart out, destroys it, that it doesn't even feel like it ever belonged there in the first place? How can you recover from a book that makes your heart feel <i>wrong</i> and <i>heavy</i>?<br/><br/>Well, <b>you don't.</b><br/><br/>Stolen made me realize I had one of those things all those other humans have. A <i>heart</i> <s>only for Ty of course.</s><br/><br/>What I loved about this book was Ty. Yes I know what he did was wrong, but the way the auth</span>
  <span id="freeText17892817275658504695" style="display:none">BR with my girl <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069-pragya" rel="nofollow noopener">Pragya!</a> <s>I can't belive she feels nothing for Ty.</s> <br /><br />How can you recover from a book that rips your heart out, destroys it, that it doesn't even feel like it ever belonged there in the first place? How can you recover from a book that makes your heart feel <i>wrong</i> and <i>heavy</i>?<br /><br />Well, <b>you don't.</b><br /><br />Stolen made me realize I had one of those things all those other humans have. A <i>heart</i> <s>only for Ty of course.</s><br /><br />What I loved about this book was Ty. Yes I know what he did was wrong, but the way the author wrote his character, makes your heart hurt for him. Our brains just don't point out the fact that he <br /><i>kidnapped</i> a living, breathing human being, and kept her in a place against her will. Instead we feel for Ty, sympathize him for what he went through and find ourselves thinking how everything would be better if Gemma just gave him the love he wanted. <br /><br />Ty isn't like our typical kidnapper who kidnaps girls, threatens her parents, enjoys raping her and torturing her. He just thought that she would be much happier with him in that place. He thought that if they loved each other and if they stay together in the middle of nowhere they would be happy. He didn't want to hurt Gemma, he didn't want to <i>touch</i> her and torture her, but he <i>kidnapped</i> her and kept her in the middle of nowhere with him and that's definitely not okay.<br /><br />Still, as you read about him, he's nothing but a broken human being in need of love and care and god damn did he make my <b>eyes sweat.</b> No matter what he did, I felt pity and hurt for him. And how many times did I wish Gemma just loved him and made everything better. <br /><br />Sorry this wasn't much of a great review, but honestly I just don't know what to write for this book.<br /><br />Take all the stars Ty. All of 'em. <br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br />Reaction to finishing this:<br /><br />So like, I finished this. <br /><br />And it feels like someone squeezed my fucking heart and then poked it with needles then put a fucking boulder on my heart and it fucking <i>hurts.</i><br /><br />I don't know if I'll be able to write a review for this because I'm just <i>not okay.</i><br /><br />And the cause is<br /><br />fucking <i>Ty.</i> Yes my heart hurts for him and I loved him the most.</span>

<div id="review_2314459473" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2314459473" />
    <a title="Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com"><img alt="Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570843185p2/70316517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2314459473?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️" href="/user/show/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com">Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=tear-jerkers">tear-jerkers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=alphas">alphas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=captive-romance">captive-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=angst">angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=dark-romance">dark-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2314459473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12935846263096399885"><b>Very different from what I expected and much better!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577678272i/28686542._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I expected this to be a “Captive” Romance, where the Hero takes the heroine and treats her like he owns her, she is attracted to him from the start so she falls in love with him and they eventually live happily ever after. Those books may are pretty popular though pretty messed up, but as long as the heroine is attracted to the Hero and doesn’t actual fight him off it can all end up ok (in a romance novel). <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1577678272ra/28686543.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>However this book was so different th</span>
  <span id="freeText12935846263096399885" style="display:none"><b>Very different from what I expected and much better!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577678272i/28686542._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I expected this to be a “Captive” Romance, where the Hero takes the heroine and treats her like he owns her, she is attracted to him from the start so she falls in love with him and they eventually live happily ever after. Those books may are pretty popular though pretty messed up, but as long as the heroine is attracted to the Hero and doesn’t actual fight him off it can all end up ok (in a romance novel). <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1577678272ra/28686543.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However this book was so different than anything I ever expected, and so much better. It almost reads like a true story of a kidnapping. The the book is written from the POV of the heroine Gemma as a letter to Ty, the man that took her. It is in chronological order from right before she is kidnapped from the Bangkok airport as she is traveling with her parents and has an argument with them while they wait near the gate for their plane. <br><br>Gemma goes to an airport coffee shop to cool down and since it is full, she ends up sitting with a hands on guy after he pays for her drink when she doesn’t have any Bangkok currency. The man is Ty and he drugs her coffee and takes her outside behind some bushes and helps her change clothes and then smuggles her onto a different flight claiming she had too much to drink.<br> <br>I don’t want to give away any more than that other than to say that Gemma hates Ty, but then eventually comes to understand and need him, possibly even have feelings for him. Ty is an odd character who is both a gentleman and a captor at times. Though he does want Gemma to want to be with him. So he gives her a separate bedroom and sometimes lets her have her way, but in the end it is only to teach her a lesson when she doesn’t believe the things he tells her and how dangerous it can be.<br><br>I was in tears at some points, because of Gemma’s struggles and the fact that I genuinely liked Ty and felt bad for him when she would say certain things that would hurt his feelings. He really just loves Gemma and wants her to see the beauty of the land and to love him back. I really ended up hoping for that to happen. Which is really crazy considering he was a stranger who kidnapped her from an airport.<br><br><a href="https://www.ilikebooksbest.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a>|<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/wennel" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a>|<a href="https://www.facebook.com/ilikebooksbest" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>|<a href="https://www.instagram.com/ilikebooksbest" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a>|<a href="https://www.twitter.com/wendysu020202" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>|<a href="https://www.bookbub.com/profile/1895823057" rel="nofollow noopener">BookBub</a></span>
