<div id="review_563460377" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/563460377" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/563460377?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer563460377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14205200930179877946"><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/3cd3931a-0e56-4078-83bb-2a12991c4aff_zpsfa8f7ac0.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413728i/814999._SX540_.jpg' alt=' photo 3cd3931a-0e56-4078-83bb-2a12991c4aff_zpsfa8f7ac0.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Okay... I just finished this book and I need to take some deep breaths and calm down a little- alright, here it goes! <br/><br/>Sixteen year old Gemma is at an airport coffee shop in Bangkok when she sees him. Ty is in his mid twenties. He looks familiar to her, something about his beautiful blue eyes, but she can’t place him. He buys her a coffee, they chat, then she starts to feel funny. She has been drugged. She is being kidnapped. <br/><br/>Now, meet Ty and Gemma:<br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/d44026e7-e26e-4a7d-8ebd-aefd31ce0ab0_zpsf48da3d7.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413728i/815000._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo d44026e7-e26e-4a7d-8ebd-aefd31ce0ab0_zpsf48da3d7.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/2b169280-44bc-4828-8493-478c6726a779_zps6c3dbf48.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413728i/815001.jpg' alt=' photo 2b169280-44bc-4828-8493-478c6726a779_zps6c3dbf48.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>When Gemma comes to, she is surprise</span>
  <span id="freeText14205200930179877946" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/3cd3931a-0e56-4078-83bb-2a12991c4aff_zpsfa8f7ac0.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413728i/814999._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo 3cd3931a-0e56-4078-83bb-2a12991c4aff_zpsfa8f7ac0.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Okay... I just finished this book and I need to take some deep breaths and calm down a little- alright, here it goes! <br><br>Sixteen year old Gemma is at an airport coffee shop in Bangkok when she sees him. Ty is in his mid twenties. He looks familiar to her, something about his beautiful blue eyes, but she can’t place him. He buys her a coffee, they chat, then she starts to feel funny. She has been drugged. She is being kidnapped. <br><br>Now, meet Ty and Gemma:<br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/d44026e7-e26e-4a7d-8ebd-aefd31ce0ab0_zpsf48da3d7.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413728i/815000._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo d44026e7-e26e-4a7d-8ebd-aefd31ce0ab0_zpsf48da3d7.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/2b169280-44bc-4828-8493-478c6726a779_zps6c3dbf48.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413728i/815001.jpg" alt=" photo 2b169280-44bc-4828-8493-478c6726a779_zps6c3dbf48.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>When Gemma comes to, she is surprised. She isn’t tied up, the doors aren’t locked. She is just in a bed in a house in the middle of nowhere. There is desert and sand everywhere, but nothing else. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/00726e41-05fd-4243-9f3c-c115ccbca694_zps077ba395.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413728i/815002.jpg" alt=" photo 00726e41-05fd-4243-9f3c-c115ccbca694_zps077ba395.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>She tries to escape, but Ty explains to her that there is nothing close, they are hundreds of miles away from any kind of civilization. She has so many questions: Why her? What does Ty want from her, how long is he planning on keeping her here?<br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/710024a2-1fa1-4bb5-8ba3-6330920565cf_zpse8289f6c.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413728i/815003.jpg" alt=" photo 710024a2-1fa1-4bb5-8ba3-6330920565cf_zpse8289f6c.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Gemma soon realizes that Ty is not the guy she thought he was. Ty actually first met Gemma when she was 10. He loves Gemma, he wants her, and only her, forever. Gemma has a hard time dealing with this. It takes her a long time to understand and trust Ty. She wants her freedom, she wants to leave, and many times- she tries to escape.<br><br>The desert is a beautiful but scary place, trying to escape this secluded place can be more dangerous than staying. Its very hot during the day, and very cold in the evening. But Gemma is strong. She is determined, and I loved her for that. But eventually, Ty started to wear her down. She saw that Ty wasn’t a monster. He was just a lonely guy with some issues who truly did love her. He also does something not many kidnappers would ever do... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Because he loves her and wants her to be happy, he gives her a promise. Stay with him for 4 more months, and he will let her go if she really wants to. Deep down, I believe if they would have made it to the 4 month mark, and she still would have wanted to go- he would have let her. No matter how much he loved her and wanted her to stay. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>And she started to have feelings for him as well, towards the end. <br><b>
  <blockquote>And you expected me to love you. And that's the hardest bit. Because I did, or at least, I loved something out there.<br>But I hated you too. I can't forget that</blockquote>
</b> I’m going to just put it out there that I LOVE TY! Yes, I know he is a kidnapper, but he is not a bad guy. Ty’s history/background made him the person he is. I sympathized with him. He is sweet, kind, beautiful, and its really hard not to like him- in his head <b>everything</b> he did was for Gemma, because he loves her. You can’t fault him for that. My favorite reason TY IS AMAZING <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[At the end, he chose to SAVE GEMMA and stayed with her when he could have just left her at the clinic and got away. She wanted him to stay, so he did. BECAUSE HE LOVED HER. He risked his life, going to prison, all of it- just to be by her side. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Amazing. <br><br>Right around the time Gemma realizes she has some kind of feelings for Ty, something bad happens <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She gets bit by a poisonous snake and Ty has to take her for help. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>The ending... oh boy that ending. I just didn’t want it to end there. I NEED MORE!!! Yes I was crying, crying like a little baby... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ After the kiss Gemma and Ty shared, I really had hope she would try to get him out of this, but the ending didn’t show that happening. :(  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><b>
  <blockquote>All I could think about was you. I wanted you in the apartment. I wanted your arms around me, your face close to mine. I wanted your smell. And I knew I couldn’t - <i>shouldn’t</i> - have it. That’s what I hated most. The uncertainty of you. You’d kidnapped me, put my life in danger . . . but I loved you, too.</blockquote>
</b><br>I don’t even know how to conclude this review... Honestly, I probably should have waited a few days to write this one because my head is all over the place and I am so full of emotion, but I just wanted to put it out there. I loved this book, I loved Ty, and I want a sequel. If you haven’t read this one, you should. It is unlike any other kidnapping/captured book I have ever read. It’s one of those I know will stay with me. I also thought the way it was written was interesting, all from Gemma’s pov as a letter to Ty. A 5 star book for me I would HIGHLY recommend!<br><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/a6550c83-127b-497c-b251-c26eb79170f1_zps5ba63500.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413728i/815004.jpg" alt=" photo a6550c83-127b-497c-b251-c26eb79170f1_zps5ba63500.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14205200930179877946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer398426021" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10880965736157125263"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “How long will you keep me?" I asked.<br/>You shrugged. "Forever, of course.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br/><br/><b>ATTENTION PLEASE!!!</b><br/><br/>This book is <b>FANTASTIC</b>. <br/><br/>WHY? because it's <b>UNIQUE</b>, and it's <b>not usual KIDNAPPING STORY.</b> It's something else entirely, and it's <b>WORTHY OF YOUR TIME.</b><br/><br/>Stolen is also quite <b>REALISTIC, CREEPY</b> and <b>EXCELLENT STORY.</b> <br/><br/><br/>And, the one thing that made me love it is <b>THE UNIQUE WAY OF WRITING.</b> This is a letter... <b>a LETTER TO HER CAPTOR - LITERALLY.</b> And it's <b> ENDING </b> was what <b> i loved the</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10880965736157125263" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “How long will you keep me?" I asked.<br>You shrugged. "Forever, of course.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br><br><b>ATTENTION PLEASE!!!</b><br><br>This book is <b>FANTASTIC</b>. <br><br>WHY? because it's <b>UNIQUE</b>, and it's <b>not usual KIDNAPPING STORY.</b> It's something else entirely, and it's <b>WORTHY OF YOUR TIME.</b><br><br>Stolen is also quite <b>REALISTIC, CREEPY</b> and <b>EXCELLENT STORY.</b> <br><br><br>And, the one thing that made me love it is <b>THE UNIQUE WAY OF WRITING.</b> This is a letter... <b>a LETTER TO HER CAPTOR - LITERALLY.</b> And it's <b> ENDING </b> was what <b> i loved the most</b>. This story also has *serious spoiler* <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ no HEA which is why it's so realistic.... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br><b>The characters were fabulous </b> and you understand both Ty and Gemma completely and utterly. <b>The less you know of story, the better, </b> which is why i won't write any synopsis for it :)<br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>CHARACTERS</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Gemma</u>
  </i>
</b>:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “It was like I existed in a kind of parallel universe, thinking thoughts and feelings that no one else understood.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br><br><br><br>Gemma..sweet Gemma... Gemma who made a mistake... She is the type of the girl which is persistent, not a quitter and still hopeful... I have to applaud her for being one of the strongest heroines ever, even when she herself never felt that way. She was full of courage and she never stopped fighting... She was scared, and i was scared with her. <br><br><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Ty</u>
  </i>
</b>:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “People love what they're used to, I guess."<br>"No." You shook your head. "People should love what needs loving. That way they can save it.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br><br>I hated him in the beginning, to me he was just too insane... until i understood him, just like Gemma. I cannot even begin to describe how i felt about him... And even when i learned of his past...his actions still weren't right...and i cannot forgive him for that. Which leads to simple fact that he never understood right from wrong...<br><br>And it made it easier for him to plan all of this (and it took <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ 6 years...Were were talking about his sanity right? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>).<br><br>But, i have to say that in the end, i did like him, because of one thing: <i> He never made her do something against her will, except to stay with him. </i><br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>OVERALL</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>I just loved it. And i will love it always, because its the most unique story i have read for a while, and there were so many feelings involved which is why this story deserves no less than five stars.<br>I highly recommend it!!!!</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “I mean, that star over there is blinking at me madly now, but for how long? An hour or two, or for the next million years? And how long will we sit here like this? Just another moment, or the rest of our lives? You know which one I'd prefer...” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br><br><b>
  <i>This review can be found on my blog: <a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">infinity-of-time.blogspot.com</a> also known as... </i>

<div id="review_1735817469" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1735817469" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1735817469?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1735817469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9192964221979141209"><b> You saw me before I saw you. In the airport, that day in August, you had that look in your eyes, as though you wanted something from me, as though you'd wanted it for a long time. No one had ever looked at me like that before, with that kind of intensity. It unsettled me, surprised me, I guess. Those blue, blue eyes, icy blue, looking back at me as if I could warm them up. They're pretty powerful, you know, those eyes, pretty beautiful too.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471892272i/20121271.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So as you can read from the blurb, this book is written</span>
  <span id="freeText9192964221979141209" style="display:none"><b> You saw me before I saw you. In the airport, that day in August, you had that look in your eyes, as though you wanted something from me, as though you'd wanted it for a long time. No one had ever looked at me like that before, with that kind of intensity. It unsettled me, surprised me, I guess. Those blue, blue eyes, icy blue, looking back at me as if I could warm them up. They're pretty powerful, you know, those eyes, pretty beautiful too.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471892272i/20121271.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So as you can read from the blurb, this book is written like a letter from Gemma to her captor. It mostly just tells the whole story. <br><br>This book brought out quite a few feels from me. Here is this hot guy that steals Gemma away from the airport and her family. NOT GOOD!<br><br>Here is a hot guy that takes her to Australia.<br>Here is a hot guy that DOESN'T rape her. <br>Here is a hot guy with a lot of issues from LIFE.<br>Here is a hot guy that has been watching Gemma for many years. <br>Here is the same hot guy that saved Gemma from being raped, but she didn't know it until he took her. <br><br><b>"How long have you been planning it?"<br>You shrugged. "Awhile, two or three years. But I'd been watching you for longer than that."<br>"How long?"<br>"About six years."<br>"Since I was ten? You've been watching me since then?"<br>You nodded. "On and off."<br>"I don't believe you," I said. But something inside me was telling me to think about it. There was something there, at the back of my mind that, if I thought about it a little more, might make sense of all this.</b><br><br>Over time, Ty tells Gemma about when they first met and how and it was really sad and sweet. I don't want to tell you about that. Ty also tells Gemma when he decided he wanted her in his life forever. Of course taking her against her will and making her live with him isn't the right way to go! <br><br>Ty was crazy, so many of us are and he had some weird ways, but those ways were just who he was, how he expressed himself. Now I'm just talking about Ty the person, not the guy that stole a girl to live and love forever. He was expressive in beautiful ways, he could see the good in nature and little things, he was always kind to Gemma even when she was trying to run away or when she would attack him. He just wanted to live alone on his land with her and try to have a life together. He was making things up really well considering. I mean living off the grid and all. <br><br>He just needed to get his head on right and maybe over the years tried to have talked to her and not steal her away. Oh well, then we would have a different book. <br><br>Ty asked Gemma if she would just stay there for 6 months and see how she felt after that. Gemma said she would for four months. He would then let her go if she didn't love where they lived and didn't want to stay there. But then something stupid happens and he has to get her to a hospital. And that was it. That is the one thing that irritated me about the book. I wanted to see what all would happen in the four months. But Ty risked being taken to jail in order to save Gemma's life and at the end there, Gemma started to like Ty when she started to just listen to him and they talked. <br><br>No matter what would have happened, there would always be that thought. . . well I have fallen in love with you now, but you stole me you arse! How would you even work with that? I guess the one good thing is that she got stolen by a nice guy and not someone who raped and tortured her to death! <br><br>And in the end, it doesn't really matter what I think or what you think. We just love books and we don't all love or understand the same books! And I could care less as long as we are all happy with something! <br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/08/stolen-by-lucy-christopher.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9192964221979141209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_459503062" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/459503062" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13247178-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473718933p2/13247178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/459503062?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/13247178-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it

              <span id="reviewTextContainer459503062" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17196478119682870522"><br/><b>♥ 5 CAPTIVATINGLY BEAUTIFUL STARS. ♥</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"You saw me before I saw you..."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398184i/769321.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Where to even begin with a review on a story like this...</b><br/><br/>Let me start off by saying that this was <i>not</i> an easy story to read. From the moment I started reading it, I felt like there were dark clouds looming over me and something bad was going to happen any minute. And I pretty much felt that way throughout the entire book, which explains exactly why I was so hesitant to start it at first. But in the end, I'm really gl</span>
  <span id="freeText17196478119682870522" style="display:none"><br><b>♥ 5 CAPTIVATINGLY BEAUTIFUL STARS. ♥</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"You saw me before I saw you..."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398184i/769321.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Where to even begin with a review on a story like this...</b><br><br>Let me start off by saying that this was <i>not</i> an easy story to read. From the moment I started reading it, I felt like there were dark clouds looming over me and something bad was going to happen any minute. And I pretty much felt that way throughout the entire book, which explains exactly why I was so hesitant to start it at first. But in the end, I'm really glad I finally did give this fascinating story a try because I ended up loving it and I've definitely found myself a new author to put on my favorite authors list.<br><br><b>Stolen</b> is written as a letter from the kidnapped young girl, Gemma, to the man who took her from her family and the life she knew, Ty. The way the author has written it, the story seems much more realistic than many other captivity stories I've read so far.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398184i/769322._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When sixteen year old is on vacation with her parents, she meets the charming and trustworthy looking twenty-five year old Ty in a coffee shop at Bangkok Airport. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"It's funny, but I always thought I could trust blue eyes. I thought they were safe somehow. All the good guys have baby blues. The dark eyes are for the villains...the Grim Reaper, the Joker, zombies. All dark."</b>
</blockquote><br><br>But not Ty...his eyes were the perfect blue, the kind of blue that sucks you in and pulls you under its spell before you realize it's too late. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398184i/769323._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>♢ <b>He makes her trust him.<br>♢ He deceives her. <br>♢ He steals her.<br>♢ And he takes her. <br>♢ Far, far away.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398184i/769324._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He takes her to the Sandy desert in Australia.<br><br>A place so isolated, so devoid of any human existence that there's no way for Gemma to reach to anyone for help...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398184i/769325.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Gemma is not an easy victime. She's a strong, admirable heroine and she tries to fight Ty every chance she's got. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[At times, I even thought she was a bit too harsh towards him, but then I of course remembered what he did in the first place... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Although, Gemma <i>hates</i> her new living conditions at first, she does start to appreciate the wonders of nature a bit more every day. She even starts to get attached to tha camel Ty has caught and decided to keep around as a mode of transportation.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398184i/769326._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And Gemma <i>certainly</i> hates her captor too. She makes it perfectly clear to him too. But along the way she also starts to understand where he's coming from more and more...<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"You were stupid and evil and mentally ill. That was all. When you started talking, you started changing."</b>
</blockquote><br><br>When Ty begins to open up to Gemma about his past, she starts to see him in a different light. He becomes more than just her kidnapper. Becomes of everything they go through together, she starts to get attached to him in a way too, but I wouldn't call it Stockholm Syndrom exactly. I think it's normal for anyone to start to form a connection to the person you're in such close proximity with for such a long time and who essentially treats you with kindness and respect most of the time too.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"That's what I hated most. The uncertainty of you. You kidnapped me, put my life in danger...but I loved you too. Or thought I did. None of it made sense."</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398184i/769327.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is not only a story about kidnapping or dispair or being forced to live in the harsh surroundings of the Australian desert. It is also a story about hope, love and forgiveness. It's a story about being forced to readapt, to start over a whole new life a,D being able to make it work out for the best. It's also a story about the power of nature and of finding beauty in living of the land that nature gave us, with not much luxury to accompany it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398184i/769328._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Although the story ends with sort of an open ending, it still made me really *really* sad in a way. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I just couldn't help but feel sorry for Ty. What he did was terribly wrong and there's no excuse for the way he handled things. But I do think it's sad that someone like him, who wanted nothing more than to be one with nature, was reduced to spending his days in a small cell. The fact that he gave up on his dream to live out in the wild in order to accompany Gemma to the hospital show just how much he really did love her and was prepared to give up his freedom for her. That makes his actions a bit more redeemable, in my opinion. And I really hoped the judge would give him a punishment accordingly, instead of looking him up in a windowless room. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I would have loved for there to be a sequel or maybe a short novella about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[how the process would have ended <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but like I said, I'm more than okay with it being an open ending as well.<br><br><p><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398184ra/769329.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All I have left to say is that this story will, with absolute certainty, stay with me for a very long time. Even now, days after finishing it, I still often think about it. <i>Stolen</i> is a unique novel with a very powerful message that I would <b>highly recommend</b> <i>everyone</i> to read and hopefully end up loving just as much as I did!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398184i/769330._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></p></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_614533482" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/614533482" />
    <a title="Navessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa"><img alt="Navessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444162983p2/18104163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/614533482?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navessa" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa">Navessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=insufferable-mc">insufferable-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=poorly-executed-strong-theme">poorly-executed-strong-theme</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=trolls-love-me">trolls-love-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=books-everyone-loves-but-i-hate">books-everyone-loves-but-i-hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=male-lead-needs-to-be-maced">male-lead-needs-to-be-maced</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer614533482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14425984141306316498">This book. I read it. And it gave me feels. Sometimes the narrative. Drove me crazy. Sometimes The Ty. Drove me crazy. Sometimes The Gemma. Drove me crazy. Sometimes The Camel. Made me laugh. <br/><br/>Okay, in all seriousness, if anyone wants a test for how much “crazy” they have, this book is it. All you have to do is find a piece of paper and something to write with and start making strike marks for every scene in which Gemma <i>should</i> attempt to KILL Ty. I think I got up to 27 or so, with each murder bec</span>
  <span id="freeText14425984141306316498" style="display:none">This book. I read it. And it gave me feels. Sometimes the narrative. Drove me crazy. Sometimes The Ty. Drove me crazy. Sometimes The Gemma. Drove me crazy. Sometimes The Camel. Made me laugh. <br><br>Okay, in all seriousness, if anyone wants a test for how much “crazy” they have, this book is it. All you have to do is find a piece of paper and something to write with and start making strike marks for every scene in which Gemma <i>should</i> attempt to KILL Ty. I think I got up to 27 or so, with each murder becoming more devious and creative than the last. Concerning, I know. I’m thinking about seeking professional help. <br><br>Speaking of the man Gemma should have MURDERED, he remained a creepy, unstable bastard for me from the first page to the last. Every time I found myself starting to think that being trapped in the middle of nowhere with a rugged Aussie that, for the most part, fell somewhere in the tolerable side of the crazy/hot scale didn’t sound so bad, he’d do something truly disturbing like admit that the first time he felt attracted to her was when she had a near miss with sexual assault. Or admit that she looks like his mom. <br><br>Christian? Is that you??? NOT AGAIN!<br><br>I had a lot of issues with Gemma too but they <i>really</i> weren’t her fault. She was your average city dwelling teenage girl with ZERO survival skills. She convinces herself that writing HELP in the desert sand won’t do any good, doesn’t think that the steel of the knife she hides is greater than the muscle of Ty and deludes herself when he starts telling her how long he’s been watching her. Why? He’s obviously batshit cray-cray, HE KIDNAPPED YOU! Let the man tell you about how fucked up he is so you won’t feel so bad when you finally cave to my demands and MURDER HIM. <br><br>Also, her attempted escapes were laughable. You have all this free time and you can’t come up with anything better than running into an endless desert with no supplies or stealing a car? <br><br>Here’s a thought, your captor admitted to having enough food stockpiled to last YEARS. Choose one of the 27 ways I suggested for you to kill him, KILL HIM, find the keys to the car, the spare gas, food and water and drive your ass out of the desert. Or just KILL HIM and chillax for a bit. Either way…<b>KILL HIM.</b> <br><br>Regardless of my personal level of crazy, I was captivated by this book. I found myself constantly wondering how it would all play out, how it would end. And as much as I wanted to see that ending I wish it hadn’t come so soon. I wish the “Stockholm Syndrome” went further than it did. I feel that it really could have been explored to a greater depth. So in the end…meh. Not as good as I thought it would be but still an intriguing enough premise to warrant two stars. <br><br><br><a href="http://litchickhitlist.blogspot.com/2013/05/stolen-by-lucy-christopher.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380236610i/681458._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> </span>

<div id="review_71954497" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71954497" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71954497?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Arlene by: </span>
      Gift from Flannery - Thank you!
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=shock-n-awe">shock-n-awe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=aussie">aussie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71954497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3128151957932213040">Wow!! What an emotional, gripping and addictive book! I was hooked to this story from the beginning and despite how I knew nothing good would come of it, I drove head on collision with the conclusion and was left with a wreckage of angst and sadness.<br/><br/>But before I tell you how I really felt, excuse me a moment, while I self-reflect...<br/><br/><i>Felt an emotional pull toward the captor? Check.<br/>Believed that he deserved some semblance of happiness because of his past? Check.<br/>Recognized moments where the captor s</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3128151957932213040" style="display:none">Wow!! What an emotional, gripping and addictive book! I was hooked to this story from the beginning and despite how I knew nothing good would come of it, I drove head on collision with the conclusion and was left with a wreckage of angst and sadness.<br /><br />But before I tell you how I really felt, excuse me a moment, while I self-reflect...<br /><br /><i>Felt an emotional pull toward the captor? Check.<br />Believed that he deserved some semblance of happiness because of his past? Check.<br />Recognized moments where the captor showed love and deep emotion toward the victim? Check.<br />Justified the captor’s actions because he provided a safe haven for the victim and wanted him to have a HEA? Check.</i><br /><br />Well sweet painful HALE I think I’m a prime candidate for Stockholm Syndrome. Gah!<br /><br /> <b>Stolen</b> brought to the surface justifications I never thought I’d consider and deep feelings for Ty despite his heinous act toward Gemma. What a crafty author to be able to tamper with my moral compass without my awareness and create a story and situation where I wanted the captor to get an ending he really didn’t deserve.<br /><br />In <b>Stolen</b> Gemma is kidnapped from her family in Bangkok Airport and taken to the Australian Outback by Ty, an emotionally disturbed young man. She fights despite futile efforts to get away, but after a series of close calls, she finds herself in a situation where she starts to see Ty through a different lens, one that includes sympathy, resolve, hidden beauty and love. <br /><br />For me, I think my defenses toward Ty fell apart when he rescued Gemma from one of her escapes where she almost died in the desert. I started to wonder if there was some way these two could come to build a life together. Part of me carried some hope and the other part cringed. So much happened in this book and I think I internalized a ton of the emotion because I feel like I’ve been walking around in a daze since I started this story. <br /><br />After all was said and done, I think the author ended the story appropriately (yes, there I go again with that word, but I think it fits here) because as much as I wanted Gemma to help free Ty and give him a second chance, I realized that sometimes you must pay the price for your crime before you get your reprieve. <br /><br />This was definitely an angsty book that created conflicting emotions for me. Intense!! <br /><br />Lastly… I hope someone went back to the shack and fed the chickens. I also worried about the camel. I hope she was able to find her herd. I know… I know.. I focus on the irrelevant details, but that’s just me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3128151957932213040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

This is so refreshing because, although she is terrified after being kidnapped by a man who </span>
  <span id="freeText2863239861596715305" style="display:none">My review and discussion is up! <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZgLruwl6jN4&amp;list=UUwNqxZRSLVW0Vy6JiSh_Y3A">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZgLru...</a><br />This book has made my list of all-time favorite books! <br />The premise is so unlike any book that I've ever read and so original in its format: a letter written to the kidnapper by the 16 year old girl who was kidnapped.<br />The main character, Gemma, is a strong and capable girl who actually makes smart decisions after being kidnapped by Ty. This is so refreshing because, although she is terrified after being kidnapped by a man who has been stalking her for six years, she still tries to survive. <br />I also loved how Stockholm syndrome came into play. Everyone, including the reader, believes that Gemma is suffering from this syndrome and that is what is causing her to sympathize and later fall in love with Ty. However, I still questioned whether there was a part of Gemma that actually had fallen for him. </span>

<div id="review_445093479" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/445093479" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/445093479?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=beautiful-prose">beautiful-prose</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=books-that-linger">books-that-linger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=aussie">aussie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=teary-eyed-reads">teary-eyed-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer445093479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14270168335522368484">I literally just put down <i>Stolen</i> and my brain...it can't think. I just need to let this book sit and saturate into me, every part of me because it can and it will and I will let it. <br/><br/>I do want to say, however, that <i>Stolen</i> was not what I expected. When I went into it, I was almost expecting an eventual romance, but there is none and I'm glad there isn't. <i>Stolen</i> is a novel of abduction, but it is also a novel of hope and faith and beauty. I only really fell in love with <i>Stolen</i> seven pages from the </span>
  <span id="freeText14270168335522368484" style="display:none">I literally just put down <i>Stolen</i> and my brain...it can't think. I just need to let this book sit and saturate into me, every part of me because it can and it will and I will let it. <br /><br />I do want to say, however, that <i>Stolen</i> was not what I expected. When I went into it, I was almost expecting an eventual romance, but there is none and I'm glad there isn't. <i>Stolen</i> is a novel of abduction, but it is also a novel of hope and faith and beauty. I only really fell in love with <i>Stolen</i> seven pages from the end; until then, I was on the fence. I think, more than anything, I was <i>confused</i> while reading this, which is what you're supposed to feel... You see, this book is such a mind-fuck (excuse my language, but there is really no other better way to put it) because on one hand, you despise Ty for stealing Gemma, for taking her away from her home, for stalking her for so many years, for making her life miserable; but, at the same time, I despised Gemma whenever she destroyed Ty's art, when she hurt him with her words, when she mocked him and his love for his desert, when she failed to even try to understand him the way he so obviously understood her...<br /><br /><i>Stolen</i> isn't a romance and for 90% of the novel, Gemma is constantly trying to run away from Ty, to escape her predicament. Yet, somewhere, she realizes that some of what Ty says is true; society <i>is</i> terrible and cruel and parents really <i>don't</i> understand their children and sometimes even friends don't and terrible things <i>do</i> happen. But, that gene that tells you in your brain that you have to accept the bad things and move on, that you can't save everyone, that maybe even you can't save yourself...it wasn't in Ty. Yes, Ty steals Gemma, but he steals her because he thinks he's doing the right thing. Unknowingly, Gemma saves him as a child and he wants to return the favor. It's so mind-boggling because Ty isn't a bad person; he's nice to Gemma, he never harms her or takes advantage of her in any way, he clothes her and feeds her and shows her the beauty of the desert; but he's wrong in his own right, too. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"I can't save you like that Ty. <br /><br />What you did to me wasn't this brilliant thing, like you think it was. You took me away from everything - my parents, my friends, my life. You took me to the sand and the heat, the dirt and isolation. And you expected me to love you. And that's the hardest bit. Because I did, or at least, I loved something out there.<br /><br />But I hated you too. I can't forget that."</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>Stolen,</i> I felt, was a social commentary of sorts. It's difficult to understand and comprehend properly and it's painful because of that, because of the confusion we feel and the sudden desperation as we want to escape to a desert, see the sunset, and live alone, but happy, without the burdens of society and expectations of our parents and disappointments of our friends. In life, however, there are always two paths: the right one and the wrong one. From my experience, the wrong one is always the easiest, but leads to eventual downfall, just as the right one is full of hurdles, but ultimately leads to happiness. In <i>Stolen,</i> however, all the lines are blurred; just the way I like it in a truly fantastic novel. <br /><br />I will warn you, reading this novel is a strange experience. I felt uncomfortable, not knowing where the plot was leading, not knowing what I wanted to happen, but I feel better now that it's over. In some ways, I feel like this novel is better for a re-read than anything else, an opportunity to understand what really happened and where Gemma started to feel something more than hatred for Ty. One of the things that did surprise me, however, was how un-original Ty's story wound up being. Now, I won't say that it isn't terrible and cruel and painful, but the path that Ty took seems so much more strange than most people in his situation. I think, however, that to become a stalker like Ty, to become obsessed with a person, to think that you're saving them...you don't need to go through a unique traumatic experience for that. Anything, even something as small as six-year-old Gemma talking to him, a stranger, can alter the mind in such a way; after all, who are we to know the depths and recesses of our brains and how events can affect you? <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"It sounded weird to hear you talk so much; normally you only said a few words at a time. I'd never imagined that you'd have a story, too. Until that moment, you were just the kidnapper. You didn't have reasons for anything. You were stupid and evil and mentally ill. That was all. When you started talking, you started changing."</i>
</b><br /><br />As for me, I don't know what to think. Yes, I do think Gemma suffered from a form of Stockholm Syndrome, I do think she makes the right decision, I do think Ty is slightly insane, I do think he is a good person, I do think his axis in life is just a little off...but I don't see Ty as a monster and neither do I see Gemma as a tortured abduction victim. If anything, there is too much of a silver lining to this tale. It's sad and depressing and unhappy, but it's also right and true and beautiful. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"And, let's face it, you did steal me. But you saved my life, too. And somewhere in the middle, you showed me a place so different and beautiful, I can never get it out of my mind. And I can't get you out of there, either. You're stuck in my brain like my own blood vessels."</i>
</b> <br /><br />Lucy Christopher, I will read anything you write. Anything. Especially if it's a sequel to <i>Stolen</i> that I hope you will eventually write onto paper instead of keeping locked up in your head. I do have to admit, however, that the ending to this is perfect and it doesn't need a sequel at all. I wouldn't mind if a sequel was written, but I don't need one either. Just this gem of a novel is enough...<br /><br />I realize this is long, but it's also not much of a review, for which I apologize. It doesn't even begin to touch upon the complexity of Ty's character; his passion for the stark Australian desert, his talent with animals, his love of art, his intelligence and resourcefulness... It barely even grazes the vastness of the backdrop this book is set against, a landscape so harsh, yet lovely, that it was a deeply enigmatic character in its own right. But, all this isn't something I can just write about or explain or even begin to understand; it's something you just have to experience on your own.<br /><br />Without a doubt, I am in love with this book. It is thoughtful, compelling, and mind-numbingly provocative. It is written in a beautiful and creeping manner, molding its way around your heart all while growing thorns. Best of all, however, it makes you think and question your own life and long for something inexplicable...and, really, isn't that the most we can ask of a book? For it to impart some of itself in us, for it to make us see an author's passion, and for it to make us attempt to define that which is undefinable?<br /><br />You can read <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com/2013/01/review-stolen-by-lucy-christopher.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on my blog, <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14270168335522368484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <i>You saw me before I saw you.</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>This book was just <b>WOW</b>!I fell in love with the characters but mostly with the writing style.To be more specific , this book is written like a letter,<i>a letter to her captor</i>, which means that she is refering to him.This is very beautiful because the reader takes part in the story and the book is <b>alive</b>.<br><br>Gemma never thought that a friendly stranger could harm her.The story begins when she is in a coffee shop at the airport.There she spots a familiar face but she cant remember whether she has seen him again or not.This beautiful blond guy with those mesmerizing eyes approaches her.He is gentle and he buys her a coffee.However things didnt turn in her favor.Obviously Ty had other plans , for <b>both</b> of them.<br><br>The one moment she is speaking to him , the next she wakes up in a deserted place.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412675i/811645._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She completely freaks out with what happened.She cant help but wondering if this guy will kill her,rape her or gods knows what.However,Ty is not that guy.He didnt bring her with him to torture her but because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he loves her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and he needs company.Living in the middle of nowhere can be a little lonely sometimes.<br><br><b>“How long will you keep me?" I asked.<br>You shrugged. "Forever, of course.”</b><br><br>No matter what Ty does for her , she only thinks of ways to escape but she always ends up hurting herself.<br><br><b>"Wherever I went, you'd only catch me.<br>I couldnt get away."</b><br><br>She is trapped and she feels dead.That place is not alive but Ty tries to make her see the beauty of his world and the beauty of nature.<br>Their relationship is not easy as she cant stop thinking whether she should kill him or wait for him to kill her.It doesnt take her long though to understand that he has no intention to harm her and they start getting closer.<br><br>Dont judge me but I think that he was sick.He didnt harm her or treated her bad but his perfectly organised capture didnt take him a few months.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Hell, he was setting this up for 6 years!! <div id="review_566149244" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/566149244" />

It felt pretty generic and nothing really special. It had some action, but it still didn’t help it to be more interesting.<br/>The main character and her capture weren’t that interesting to read about, development didn't make them unique or captivating. <br/><br/>This wasn’t bad, but defiantly not memorable.<br/></span>

<div id="review_583606322" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/583606322" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/583606322?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=bad-bad-bad-romance">bad-bad-bad-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer583606322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2909819619675022359"><i>Pre-review:<br/><br/>I must confess, I'm still in the middle of the book and I'm already at the verge of giving up. <i>Stolen: A Letter to My Captor</i> annoys me so much.<br/><br/>At first I thought I'd like this story, because I'm deeply interested with Stockholm Syndrome and the conflicts between kidnapped victim and the kidnapper...and not to mention I had also tried my hand on writing yaoi fanfic with similar themes. But so far the author had failed to get the job done. If Ms. Lucy Christopher didn't redeem her creat</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2909819619675022359" style="display:none"><i>Pre-review:<br><br>I must confess, I'm still in the middle of the book and I'm already at the verge of giving up. <i>Stolen: A Letter to My Captor</i> annoys me so much.<br><br>At first I thought I'd like this story, because I'm deeply interested with Stockholm Syndrome and the conflicts between kidnapped victim and the kidnapper...and not to mention I had also tried my hand on writing yaoi fanfic with similar themes. But so far the author had failed to get the job done. If Ms. Lucy Christopher didn't redeem her creation before the ending, I would write an Angry Letter to both <s>Ty</s> Selfish Creepy Kidnapper and Ms. Christopher after I'm done.<br><br>If you are looking for some worthy drama between kidnapper and his captive, I suggest you to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1074815.The_Collector" rel="nofollow noopener">The Collector</a> instead.<br><br>And here's my reaction to Tyler MacFarlane <s>the evil kidnapper.</s><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379731761i/25209.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Need I say more?<br><br>When the review arrives, <b>please be prepared for a lot of cursing and swearing.</b> I can't help myself, I am too angry to settle for using half-heartened curses such as "freaking" and the like this time. <br><br>And you know what? I had dealt with YA creepers such as Edward Cullen and YA douchebags such as Jace Lightwood/Wayland/whatever before, but none of them had ever driven me so mad... </i><br><br><b>the actual review: penned after I'd finished the book</b><br><br><b>Rating: 2.5 stars for this book. </b><br><br>Let me tell you once more that at the beginning, I had expected myself to like this book, the writing is quite good even though I have my doubt about the subject matter: <b>"What? That dude kidnaps this girl and he expects her to love him? And it's supposed to be a Young Adult book?!"</b><br><br>To be honest, the plot of Stolen sounds more like those online erotica which I can easily found on many different NC-17 websites.<br><br>So, how does the story actually turn out?<br><br>In fact this is a difficult book to rant,I like the opening of the story, and Gemma, the kidnapped victim's struggle to grip onto her sanity and how she made her final decision. I also like the author's description of wildness of the Australian Outback. These are the bright-spots of the book. Plus I appreciate the author for NOT sugarcoating Ty, the kidnapper into some dreamboat or attractive bad boy, in fact she had made it quite clear that what the kidnapper did was wrong.<br><br>However, I'm pissed off that in the middle of the story, the author had made a handful of clumsy attempts to draw readers' sympathy to Ty by giving him one big fat sorry-ass backstory. <b>I'M VERY SORRY, BUT YOU CAN'T JUSTIFY KIDNAPPING AND STALKING WITH A BAD, FUCKED UP CHILDHOOD,PERIOD. I REFUSE TO BUY THIS GUILT TRAP, MS. CHRISTOPHER!</b><br><br>I'm equally pissed off by how unrealistic many of the details and setting are in the book. The author, Ms. Christopher had made Gemma's kidnapping in Bangkok airport and she being spirited away to the Australian Outback sound <i>ways too easy.</i> Plus I can't believe Ty, an orphan who had been fending for himself ever since he was 19 years old could somehow manage to buy a farmhouse and stored whatever food and supplies he needed in it. Not only buying the farm, Ty, a homeless teenager, somehow also managed to afford staying in British for years and stalking Gemma in his spare time, AND he also managed to afford buying plane tickets, fake ID, fake passport and a truck for his kidnapping plan. Wow, none of these seem to be realistic to me.<br><br>Gemma and Ty's characters also do nothing to redeem this story for me. Although I appreciate Gemma for not giving up and actually fighting back, still from start to end I don't have a grip on her personality and for many times she comes off as a bit of a whinny. She seems to be unhappy with her life, her parents and friends but she never clearly explains what her problem with them is, <b>SO WHAT IS SHE COMPLAINING ABOUT ANYWAY!?</b><br><br>On the other hand, Ty makes me so mad that I want to knock his skull in while screaming <b>"DIE! FUCKER, DIE!"</b> for being such a totally selfish and creepy kidnapper. <b>WHO ARE YOU? WHO GAVE YOU THE RIGHT TO KIDNAP A GIRL SO YOU CAN *SAVE* HER FROM HER FAKE, PATHETIC LIFE!!!????</b> I don't care if a kidnapper cried in his sleep, I don't care whether he is emotionally vulnerable or not, I only care about him lying to a girl and telling her that her parents are selfish and don't love her enough to come looking for her; I only care about him being arrogant enough to think he can steal a girl and CHANGE her for the better. And because he is such an irredeemable fucker, I find it unacceptable for Gemma to moon over Ty, his well built body and the supposed "wonders" he had showed her. She really disgusted me at this point.<br><br>I also can't stand Ty's cornering Gemma by surrounding the farm with chicken's fences like he is trapping some animal. <b>Goodness, this fucker makes me sick. </b>Therefore you can imagine how much shock I was in <b>when I saw on discussion board that some readers actually blame Gemma for being "heartless" toward Ty. OMG! WHAT ALTERNATIVE UNIVERSE ARE YOU FOLKS LIVING IN!?</b><br><br>Aside from Ty's unacceptable behaviors, I also don't think Ty's character is well built, and as a kidnapper he isn't even realistic. It looks like the author couldn't decide what to do with him, therefore sometime he becomes this lonely lost boy who only wants Gemma's company, sometime the author seems to want us to feel bad for Ty even though his actions (lying to Gemma about her parents, stalking her, forcing her to do things she doesn't want to, etc) show that he clearly has the making of a cold blooded criminal. Damn, that's so messed up.<br><br>Last but not least, Stolen is supposed to be a long letter written by Gemma to Ty, but this "letter format" writing doesn't work. Gemma's voice sounds too cool, level-headed and distant, which doesn't look convening given how much the girl had gone through.<br><br>Once again, I suggest you to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1074815.The_Collector" rel="nofollow noopener">The Collector</a> instead. It's a much worthy read.<br><br>PSS: A wonderful article by a fellow Goodreads friend: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://openmindedskeptic.blogspot.hk/2013/07/stolen.html#more">http://openmindedskeptic.blogspot.hk/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2909819619675022359" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2678514830" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2678514830" />
    <a title="Carrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie"><img alt="Carrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415677371p2/36817401.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2678514830?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie">Carrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11180068-stolen">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2678514830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18032871735437211852">Stolen: A Letter to My Captor by Lucy Christopher is a young adult contemporary novel. This one is, as the subtitle alludes to, written in the form of one long letter. Sixteen year old Gemma is basically telling her entire kidnapping experience afterwards and as one might guess the story is one that deals with Stockholm Syndrome, or the development of feelings for one’s captor.<br/><br/>Gemma had been traveling with her parents when they had a stop in the Bangkok Airport. Of course as with most sixteen ye</span>
  <span id="freeText18032871735437211852" style="display:none">Stolen: A Letter to My Captor by Lucy Christopher is a young adult contemporary novel. This one is, as the subtitle alludes to, written in the form of one long letter. Sixteen year old Gemma is basically telling her entire kidnapping experience afterwards and as one might guess the story is one that deals with Stockholm Syndrome, or the development of feelings for one’s captor.<br /><br />Gemma had been traveling with her parents when they had a stop in the Bangkok Airport. Of course as with most sixteen year olds Gemma wanted a few minutes off on her own so she asks to go get a coffee, what could possibly happen right? Well, as Gemma is in line for the coffee Ty makes his move and the older “cute” guy of course catches her attention. This leads to Gemma being drugged and smuggled out of Bangkok to a remote area in Australia.<br /><br />As dark as the subject matter of a young girl being drugged and kidnapped may be the story in here is actually a rather clean one, no worries about steamy content. Of course we start off with a scared and determined to get away Gemma but as it goes on her feelings change. This was actually quite compelling to read and even as a reader I began to feel sorry for Ty making Gemma’s feelings all the more realistic. I wouldn’t call this a romance though, it’s still very much what it was in someone being held hostage but it’s a good fictional look at how Stockholm Syndrome could come about.<br /><br />For more reviews please visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://carriesbookreviews.com/">https://carriesbookreviews.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18032871735437211852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115457010?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nic" href="/user/show/2813423-nic">Nic</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=aussie-ya">aussie-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=bookers-challenge">bookers-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115457010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15835459160008399708"><b>Favourite Quote:</b> <i>"Lets face it, you did steal me. But you saved my life too. And somewhere in the middle, you showed me a place so different and beautiful, I can never get it out of my mind. And I can't get you out of there either. You're stuck in my brain like my own blood vessels."</i><br/><br/>Stolen is one huge emotional rollercoaster ride. It had my stomach all tied up in knots and made my heart ache but it was AMAZING. Truly, a stunning and thought provoking read. <br/><br/>Lucy Christopher is a brilliant writer.</span>
  <span id="freeText15835459160008399708" style="display:none"><b>Favourite Quote:</b> <i>"Lets face it, you did steal me. But you saved my life too. And somewhere in the middle, you showed me a place so different and beautiful, I can never get it out of my mind. And I can't get you out of there either. You're stuck in my brain like my own blood vessels."</i><br /><br />Stolen is one huge emotional rollercoaster ride. It had my stomach all tied up in knots and made my heart ache but it was AMAZING. Truly, a stunning and thought provoking read. <br /><br />Lucy Christopher is a brilliant writer. She really get you thinking about what is right and wrong and the place in between. The plot was intense and captivating just like the characters. Stolen is a story that you get emotionally invested in. And the way Christopher vividly describes how stunningly gorgeous the land really is and how deadly it can be, makes it feel like it is another important character in this tale.<br /><br />When I think of Gemma the first word that comes to mind is brave. To be put in that situation at 16 I don't know if I could have handled it with as much strength as she did. She never gave up hope for escape even when her feelings towards Ty began to change. <br /><br />Ty, wow, what a damaged yet frighteningly beautiful soul. Even though it is written from Gemma's POV, I felt we got Ty story as well. He is a character that haunts your thoughts. I was so confused about how I felt about him. I know what he did was wrong and I should be disgusted by him but I liked him. You could see why he thought what he did was right in his head. Just thinking about him breaks my heart. <br /><br />The ending it made me cry like a baby and it hurt. I know some people will disagree with me but I really wish it could have ended another way. Yet I see that it would have been impossible.<br /><br />Stolen, is an unforgettable and breathtaking story that I highly recommend. Just make sure you are ready for a few tears.<br /><br /><i>Bookers Challenge #3 - thanks to Stefanie</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15835459160008399708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
